\\t}\\n264: }\\n265: \\n266: // SequenceValue is an omittable value in a sequence of time series values.\\n267: type SequenceValue struct {\\n268: \\tValue     float64\\n269: \\tOmitted   bool\\n270: handler that turns panics into returns from the top level of Parse.\\n343: func (*parser) recover(errp *error) {\\n344: \\te := recover()\\n345: \\tswitch _, ok := e.(runtime.Error); {\\n346: \\tcase ok:\\n347: \\t\\t// Print the stack trace but do not inhibit the running application.\\n348: \\t\\tbuf := make([]byte, 64<<10)\\n349: \\t\\tbuf = buf[:runtime.Stack(buf, false)]\\n350: \\n351: Lex is expected by the yyLexer interface of the yacc generated parser.\\n359: // It writes the next Item provided by the lexer to the provided pointer address.\\n360: // Comments are skipped.\\n361: //\\n362: // The yyLexer interface is currently implemented by the parser to allow\\n363: // the generated and non-generated parts to work together with regards to lookahead\\n364: // and error handling.\\n365: //\\n366: // For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\\n367: func (p *parser) Lex(lval *yySymType) int {\\n368: \\tvar typ ItemType\\n369: \\n370: \\tif p.injecting {\\n371: \\t\\tp.injecting = false\\n372: \\t\\treturn int(p.inject)\\n373: \\t}\\n374: \\t// Skip comments.\\n375: \\tfor {\\n376: \\t\\tp.lex.NextItem(&lval.item)\\n377: \\t\\ttyp \\treturn int(typ)\\n401: }\\n402: \\n403: // Error is expected by the yyLexer interface of the yacc generated parser.\\n404: //\\n405: // It is a no-op since the parsers error routines are triggered\\n406: // by mechanisms that allow more fine-grained control\\n407: // For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\\n408: func (*parser) Error(string) {\\n409: }\\n410: \\n411: // InjectItem allows injecting a single Item at the beginning of the token stream\\n412: // consumed by the generated parser.\\n413: // This allows having multiple start \\t\\t// This is made a function instead of a variable, so it is lazily evaluated on demand.\\n766: \\t\\topRange := func() (r posrange.PositionRange) {\\n767: \\t\\t\\t// Remove whitespace at the Parse.\n343: func (*parser) recover(errp *error) {\n344: \te := recover()\n345: \tswitch _, ok := e.(runtime.Error); {\n346: \tcase ok:\n347: \t\t// Print the stack trace but do not inhibit the running application.\n348: \t\tbuf := make([]byte, 64<<10)\n349: \t\tbuf = buf[:runtime.Stack(buf, false)]\n350: \n351: \t\tfmt.Fprintf(os.Stderr, \"parser panic: %v\\n%s\", e, buf)\n352: \t\t*errp = Item provided by the lexer to the provided pointer address.\n360: // Comments are skipped.\n361: //\n362: // The yyLexer interface is currently implemented by the parser to allow\n363: // the generated and non-generated parts to work together with regards to lookahead\n364: // and error handling.\n365: //\n366: // For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\n367: func (p *parser) Lex(lval *yySymType) int {\n368: \tvar typ ItemType\n369: \n370: \tif p.injecting {\n371: \t\tp.injecting = false\n372: \t\treturn int(p.inject)\n373: \t}\n374: \t// Skip comments.\n375: \tfor {\n376: \t\tp.lex.NextItem(&lval.item)\n377: \t\ttyp = lval.item.Typ\n378: \t\tif typ != COMMENT {\n379: \t\t\tbreak\n380: \t\t}\n381: \t}\n382: \n383: \tswitch typ {\n384: \tcase ERROR:\n385: \t\tpos := posrange.PositionRange{\n386: \t\t\tStart: p.lex.start,\n387: \t\t\tEnd:   posrange.Pos(len(p.lex.input)),\n388: \t\t}\n389: \t\tp.addParseErr(pos, errors.New(p.yyParser.lval.item.Val))\n390: \n391: \t\t// Tells yacc that this is the end of input.\n392: \t\treturn 0\n393: \tcase EOF:\n394: \t\tlval.item.Typ = EOF\n395: \t\tp.InjectItem(0)\n396: \tcase RIGHT_BRACE, RIGHT_PAREN, RIGHT_BRACKET, DURATION, NUMBER:\n397: \t\tp.lastClosing = lval.item.Pos + posrange.Pos(len(lval.item.Val))\n398: \t}\n399: \n400: \treturn int(typ)\n401: }\n402: \n403: // Error is expected by the yyLexer interface of the yacc generated parser.\n404: //\n405: // It is a no-op since the parsers error routines are triggered\n406: // by mechanisms that allow more fine-grained control\n407: // For more information, see https://pkg.go.dev/golang.org/x/tools/cmd/goyacc.\n408: func (*parser) Error(string) {\n409: }\n410: \n411: // InjectItem allows injecting a single Item at the beginning of the token stream\n412: // consumed by the generated parser.\n413: // This allows having multiple start symbols as described in\n414: // https://www.gnu.org/software/bison/manual/html_node/Multiple-start_002dsymbols.html .\n415: // Only the Lex function used by the generated parser is affected by this injected Item.\n416: // Trying to \t\t\t\toutput.CounterResetHint = histogram.GaugeType\n639: \t\t\tdefault:\n640: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing counter_reset_hint: unknown value %v\", resetHint.Typ)\n641: \t\t\t}\n642: \t\t} else {\n643: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(p.yyParser.lval.item.PositionRange(), \"error parsing counter_reset_hint: %v\", val)\n644: \t\t}\n645: \t}\n646: \n647: \tbuckets, spans := p.buildHistogramBucketsAndSpans(desc, \"buckets\", \"offset\")\n648: \toutput.PositiveBuckets = buckets\n649: \toutput.PositiveSpans = spans\n650: \n651: \tbuckets, spans = p.buildHistogramBucketsAndSpans(desc, \"n_buckets\", \"n_offset\")\n652: \toutput.NegativeBuckets = buckets\n653: \toutput.NegativeSpans = spans\n654: \n655: \treturn output\n656: }\n657: \n658: // description.\n661: func (p *parser) newHistogramSequenceValue(h *histogram.FloatHistogram) SequenceValue {\n662: \treturn SequenceValue{\n663: \t\tHistogram:           h,\n664: \t\tCounterResetHintSet: p.lastHistogramCounterResetHintSet,\n665: \t}\n666: }\n667: \n668: func (p *parser) buildHistogramBucketsAndSpans(desc *map[string]any, bucketsKey, offsetKey string,\n669: ) (buckets []float64, spans []histogram.Span) {\n670: \tbucketCount := 0\n671: \tval, ok := (*desc)[bucketsKey]\n672: \tif ok {\n673: \t\tval, ok := val.([]float64)\n674: \t\tif ok {\n675: \t\t\tbuckets \t\t}\n680: \t}\n681: \toffset := int32(0)\n682: \tval, ok = (*desc)[offsetKey]\n683: \tif ok {\n684: \t\tval, ok := val.(int64)\n685: \t\tif ok {\n686: \t\t\toffset = int32(val)\n687: \t\t} else []histogram.Span{{Offset: offset, Length: uint32(bucketCount)}}\n693: \t}\n694: \treturn buckets, spans\n695: }\n696: \n697: // number parses a number.\n698: func (p *parser) number(val string) float64 {\n699: \tn, err := strconv.ParseInt(val, 0, 64)\n700: \tf := float64(n)\n701: \tif err != nil {\n702: \t\tf, err = strconv.ParseFloat(val, 64)\n703: \t}\n704: \tif err != nil {\n705: error if it\n711: // is not of the expected type.\n712: func (p *parser) expectType(node Node, want ValueType, context string) {\n713: \tt := p.checkAST(node)\n714: \tif t != want {\n715: \t\tp.addParseErrf(node.PositionRange(), \"expected type %s in %s, got %s\", DocumentedType(want), context, DocumentedType(t))\n716: \t}\n717: }\n718: \n719: // checkAST checks the validity of the provided AST. This includes type checking.\n720: func (p *parser) checkAST(node Node) (typ ValueType) {\n721: \t// For expressions the type is determined by their Type function.\n722: \t// Lists do not have a type but are not invalid either.\n723: \tswitch n := node.(type) {\n724: \tcase Expressions:\n725: \t\ttyp = ValueTypeNone\n726: \tcase Expr:\n727: \t\ttyp = n.Type()\n728: \tdefault:\n729: \t\tp.addParseErrf(node.PositionRange(), \"unknown node type: %T\", node)\n730: \t}\n731: \n732: \t// Recursively check correct typing for child nodes and raise\n733: \t// errors in case of bad typing.\n734: \tswitch n := node.(type) {\n735: \tcase *EvalStmt:\n736: \t\tty := p.checkAST(n.Expr)\n737: \t\tif ty == ValueTypeNone {\n738: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.Expr.PositionRange(), \"evaluation statement must have a valid expression type but got %s\", DocumentedType(ty))\n739: \t\t}\n740: \n741: \tcase Expressions:\n742: \t\tfor _, e := range n {\n743: \t\t\tty := p.checkAST(e)\n744: \t\t\tif ty == ValueTypeNone {\n745: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(e.PositionRange(), \"expression must have a valid expression type but got %s\", DocumentedType(ty))\n746: \t\t\t}\n747: \t\t}\n748: \tcase *AggregateExpr:\n749: \t\tif !n.Op.IsAggregator() {\n750: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"aggregation operator expected in aggregation expression but got %q\", n.Op)\n751: \t\t}\n752: \t\tp.expectType(n.Expr, ValueTypeVector, \"aggregation expression\")\n753: \t\tif n.Op == TOPK || n.Op == BOTTOMK || n.Op == QUANTILE || n.Op == LIMITK || n.Op == LIMIT_RATIO {\n754: \t\t\tp.expectType(n.Param, ValueTypeScalar, \"aggregation parameter\")\n755: \t\t}\n756: \t\tif n.Op == COUNT_VALUES {\n757: \t\t\tp.expectType(n.Param, ValueTypeString, \"aggregation parameter\")\n758: \t\t}\n759: \n760: \tcase *BinaryExpr:\n761: \t\tlt := p.checkAST(n.LHS)\n762: \t\trt := p.checkAST(n.RHS)\n763: \n764: \t\t// opRange returns the PositionRange of the operator part of the BinaryExpr.\n765: \t\t// This is made a function instead of a variable, so it is lazily evaluated on demand.\n766: \t\topRange := func() (r posrange.PositionRange) {\n767: \t\t\t// Remove whitespace at the beginning and end of the range.\n768: \t\t\tfor r.Start = n.LHS.PositionRange().End; isSpace(rune(p.lex.input[r.Start])); r.Start++ {\n769: \t\t\t}\n770: \t\t\tfor r.End = n.RHS.PositionRange().Start - 1; isSpace(rune(p.lex.input[r.End])); r.End-- {\n771: \t\t\t}\n772: \t\t\treturn r\n773: \t\t}\n774: \n775: \t\tif n.ReturnBool && !n.Op.IsComparisonOperator() {\n776: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"bool modifier can only be used on comparison operators\")\n777: \t\t}\n778: \n779: \t\tif n.Op.IsComparisonOperator() && !n.ReturnBool && n.RHS.Type() == ValueTypeScalar && n.LHS.Type() == ValueTypeScalar {\n780: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"comparisons between scalars must use BOOL modifier\")\n781: \t\t}\n782: \n783: \t\tif n.Op.IsSetOperator() && n.VectorMatching.Card == CardOneToOne {\n784: \t\t\tn.VectorMatching.Card = CardManyToMany\n785: \t\t}\n786: \n787: \t\tfor _, l1 := range n.VectorMatching.MatchingLabels {\n788: \t\t\tfor _, l2 := range n.VectorMatching.Include {\n789: \t\t\t\tif l1 == l2 && n.VectorMatching.On {\n790: \t\t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(opRange(), \"label %q must not occur in ON and GROUP clause at once\", l1)\n791: \t\t\t\t}\n792: \t\t\t}\n793: \t\t}\n794: \n795: \t\tif !n.Op.IsOperator() {\n796: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"binary expression does not support operator %q\", n.Op)\n797: \t\t}\n798: \t\tif lt != ValueTypeScalar && lt != ValueTypeVector {\n799: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.LHS.PositionRange(), \"binary expression must contain only scalar and instant vector types\")\n800: \t\t}\n801: \t\tif rt != ValueTypeScalar && rt != ValueTypeVector {\n802: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.RHS.PositionRange(), \"binary expression must contain only scalar and instant vector types\")\n803: \t\t}\n804: \n805: \t\tswitch {\n806: \t\tcase (lt != ValueTypeVector || rt != ValueTypeVector) && n.VectorMatching != nil:\n807: \t\t\tif len(n.VectorMatching.MatchingLabels) > 0 {\n808: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"vector matching only allowed between instant vectors\")\n809: \t\t\t}\n810: \t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.FillValues.LHS != nil || n.VectorMatching.FillValues.RHS != nil {\n811: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"filling in missing series only allowed between instant vectors\")\n812: \t\t\t}\n813: \t\t\tn.VectorMatching = nil\n814: \t\tcase n.Op.IsSetOperator(): // Both operands are Vectors.\n815: \t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.Card == CardOneToMany || n.VectorMatching.Card == CardManyToOne {\n816: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"no grouping allowed for %q operation\", n.Op)\n817: \t\t\t}\n818: \t\t\tif n.VectorMatching.Card != CardManyToMany {\n819: {\n822: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"filling in missing series not allowed for set operators\")\n823: \t\t\t}\n824: \t\t}\n825: \n826: \t\tif (lt == ValueTypeScalar || rt == ValueTypeScalar) && n.Op.IsSetOperator() {\n827: \t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"set operator %q not allowed in binary scalar expression\", n.Op)\n828: \t\t}\n829: \n830: \tcase *Call:\n831: least %d argument(s) in call to %q, got %d\", na, n.Func.Name, len(n.Args))\n840: \t\t\t} else if nargsmax := na + n.Func.Variadic; n.Func.Variadic > 0 && nargsmax < len(n.Args) {\n841: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(n.PositionRange(), \"expected at most %d argument(s) in call to %q, got %d\", nargsmax, n.Func.Name, len(n.Args))\n842: \t\t\t}\n843: \t\t}\n844: \n845: \t\tif n.Func.Name == \"info\" && len(n.Args) > 1 {\n846: \t\t\t// Check the type is correct first\n847: \t\t\tif n.Args[1].Type() != ValueTypeVector {\n848: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(node.PositionRange(), \"expected type %s len(n.Func.ArgTypes) {\n863: \t\t\t\tif n.Func.Variadic == 0 {\n864: \t\t\t\t\t// This is not a vararg function so we should not check the\n865: \t\t\t\t\t// type of the extra arguments.\n866: \t\t\t\t\tbreak\n867: \t\t\t\t}\n868: \t\t\t\ti = len(n.Func.ArgTypes) - 1\n869: \t\t\t}\n870: \t\t\tif t := p.checkAST(arg); t != n.Func.ArgTypes[i] {\n871: \t\t\t\tp.addParseErrf(arg.PositionRange(), \"expected type %s in call to function %q, got %s\", DocumentedType(n.Func.ArgTypes[i]), n.Func.Name, DocumentedType(t))\n872: \t\t\t}\n873: \t\t}\n874: pre-allocated empty vector that you may use to accumulate\n51: // output before returning it. The vectors in vals should not be returned.a\n52: //\n53: // Range vector functions need only return a vector with the right value,\n54: // the metric and timestamp are not needed.\n55: //\n56: // Instant vector functions need only return a vector with the right values and\n57: // metrics, the timestamp are not needed.\n58: //\n59: // Scalar results should be returned as the value of a sample in a Vector.\n60: type FunctionCall func(vectorVals []Vector, matrixVals Matrix, args parser.Expressions, enh *EvalNodeHelper) (Vector, annotations.Annotations)\n61: \n62: // === time() float64 ===\n63: func funcTime(_ []Vector, _ Matrix, _ parser.Expressions, enh *EvalNodeHelper) (Vector, annotations.Annotations) {\n64: \treturn Vector{Sample{\n65: \t\tF: float64(enh.Ts) / 1000,\n66: \t}}, nil\n67: }\n68: \n69: // pickOrInterpolateLeft returns the value at the left boundary of the range.\n70: // If interpolation is needed (when smoothed is true and the first sample is before the range start),\n71: // it returns the interpolated value at the left boundary; otherwise, it returns the first sample's value.\n72: func pickOrInterpolateLeft(floats []FPoint, first int, rangeStart int64, smoothed, isCounter bool) float64 {\n73: \tif smoothed && floats[first].T < rangeStart {\n74: \t\treturn interpolate(floats[first], floats[first+1], rangeStart, isCounter)\n75: \t}\n76: \treturn floats[first].F\n77: }\n78: \n79: // pickOrInterpolateRight returns the value at the right boundary of the range.\n80: // If interpolation is needed (when smoothed is true and the last sample is after the range end),\n81: // it returns the interpolated value at the right boundary; otherwise, it returns the last sample's value.\n82: func pickOrInterpolateRight(floats []FPoint, last int, rangeEnd int64, smoothed, isCounter bool) float64 {\n83: \tif smoothed && last > 0 && floats[last].T > rangeEnd {\n84: \t\treturn interpolate(floats[last-1], floats[last], rangeEnd, isCounter)\n85: \t}\n86: \treturn floats[last].F\n87: }\n88: \n89: // interpolate performs linear interpolation between two points.\n90: // If isCounter is true and there is a counter reset, it models the counter\n91: // as starting from 0 (post-reset) by setting y1 to 0.\n92: // It then calculates the interpolated value at the given timestamp.\n93: func interpolate(p1, p2 FPoint, t int64, isCounter bool) float64 {\n94: \ty1 := p1.F\n95: \ty2 := p2.F\n96: \tif isCounter && y2 < y1 {\n97: \t\ty1 = 0\n98: \t}\n99: \n100: \treturn y1 + (y2-y1)*float64(t-p1.T)/float64(p2.T-p1.T)\n101: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/prometheus/prometheus@1751685dd4f6430757ba3078a96cffeffcb2bb47/-/blob/promql/functions.go%3FL1-100"}}}

implemented in the `github.com/prometheus/prometheus` repository across the `promql/` and `promql/parser/` directories. The pipeline follows a multi-stage architecture:\\n\\n1. **Lexical Analysis** (Tokenization)\\n2. **Syntax Analysis** (Parsing with Yacc)\\n3. **Abstract Syntax Tree (AST) Construction**\\n4. **Semantic Validation** (Type checking)\\n5. **Query Execution** (via the Engine)\\n\\n## Key Components\\n\\n### Parser Interface and Implementation\\n\\n**File: `promql/parser/parse.go`**\\n\\n- **`Parser` interface**: Defines the public API for PromQL parsing with methods:\\n  - `ParseExpr(input string) (Expr, error)` - Parses a PromQL expression\\n  - `ParseMetric(input string)` - Parses metric definitions\\n  - `ParseMetricSelector(input string)` - Parses metric label selectors\\n  - `ParseMetricSelectors(matchers []string)` - Parses multiple selectors\\n  - `ParseSeriesDesc(input string)` - Parses series descriptions for testing\\n  - `RegisterFeatures(r features.Collector)` - Registers PromQL features\\n\\n- **`parser` struct**: Low-level parser implementation that:\\n  - Manages the lexer state (`lex Lexer`)\\n  - Maintains function registry (`functions map[string]*Function`)\\n  - Handles YACC-generated parser (`yyParser yyParserImpl`)\\n  - Accumulates parsing errors (`parseErrors ParseErrors`)\\n  - Supports parser pooling for efficiency\\n\\n- **`checkAST(node Node) ValueType`**: Performs semantic validation and type checking on the AST including:\\n  - Recursive type validation for all expressions\\n  - Vector/scalar type enforcement\\n  - Aggregation operator validation\\n  - Binary operator and vector matching validation\\n  - Function call argument type checking\\n  - Label matcher validation\\n\\n### Lexer Tokenizer\\n\\n**File: `promql/parser/lex.go`**\\n\\n- **`Lexer` struct**: Implements tokenization with:\\n  - Input stream management (`input string`)\\n  - Position tracking (`pos`, `start`, `width`)\\n  - State machine support (`state stateFn`)\\n  - Nesting depth tracking for parentheses, braces, brackets\\n  - String and duration literal handling\\n  - Histogram description parsing support\\n\\n- **`Item` struct**: Represents a lexical token with:\\n  - Type (`ItemType`) - enumerated token types\\n  - Position (`posrange.Pos`)\\n  - Value (`Val string`) - actual token text\\n\\n- **`ItemType` enum**: Defines all token types including:\\n  - Operators: `ADD`, `SUB`, `MUL`, `DIV`, `MOD`, `POW`\\n  - Comparison: `EQLC`, `NEQ`, `LTE`, `GTE`, `LSS`, `GTR`\\n  - Set operators: `LAND`, `LOR`, `LUNLESS`\\n  - Aggregators: `SUM`, `AVG`, `COUNT`, `MIN`, `MAX`, `TOPK`, `BOTTOMK`, `QUANTILE`, etc.\\n  - Keywords: `OFFSET`, `BY`, `WITHOUT`, `ON`, `IGNORING`, `GROUP_LEFT`, `GROUP_RIGHT`, `BOOL`\\n  - Literals: `NUMBER`, `STRING`, `DURATION`, `IDENTIFIER`\\n  - Delimiters: `LEFT_PAREN`, `RIGHT_PAREN`, `LEFT_BRACE`, `RIGHT_BRACE`, `LEFT_BRACKET`, `RIGHT_BRACKET`\\n\\n- **`NextItem(itemp *Item)`**: Advances the lexer and populates the next token\\n\\n### AST Node Definitions\\n\\n**File: `promql/parser/ast.go`**\\n\\n- **`Node` interface**: Base interface for all AST nodes with methods:\\n  - `String() string` - Returns parseable string representation\\n  - `Pretty(level int) string` - Returns prettified representation\\n  - `PositionRange() posrange.PositionRange` - Returns source position\\n\\n- **`Expr` interface**: Base interface for all expressions implementing `Node` with:\\n  - `Type() ValueType` - Returns expression result type (Vector, Scalar, Matrix, String)\\n  - `PromQLExpr()` - Marker method\\n\\n- **Expression Types**:\\n  - **`VectorSelector`**: Represents metric selection with label matchers\\n    - `Name string` - Metric name\\n    - `LabelMatchers []*labels.Matcher` - Label match conditions\\n    - `OriginalOffset`, `Offset` - Offset modifier\\n    - `Timestamp`, `StartOrEnd` - @ modifier\\n    - `Anchored`, `Smoothed` - Extended range modifiers\\n  \\n  - **`MatrixSelector`**: Range vector selection\\n    - `VectorSelector Expr` - Base vector selector\\n    - `Range time.Duration` - Range duration\\n  \\n  - **`BinaryExpr`**: Binary operations\\n    - `Op ItemType` - Operator type\\n    - `LHS, RHS Expr` - Left and right operands\\n    - `VectorMatching *VectorMatching` - Vector cardinality matching\\n    - `ReturnBool bool` - Modifier for comparison operators\\n  \\n  - **`AggregateExpr`**: Aggregation operations\\n    - `Op ItemType` - Aggregator type (SUM, AVG, COUNT, etc.)\\n    - `Expr Expr` - Expression to aggregate\\n    - `Param Expr` - Optional parameter (for TOPK, BOTTOMK, etc.)\\n    - `Grouping []string` - BY/WITHOUT labels\\n    - `Without bool` - Without vs By modifier\\n  \\n  - **`Call`**: Function calls\\n    - `Func *Function` - Function definition\\n    - `Args Expressions` - Arguments\\n  \\n  - **`SubqueryExpr`**: Subqueries with range and step\\n    - `Expr Expr` - Inner expression\\n    - `Range time.Duration` - Range duration\\n    - `Step time.Duration` - Step duration\\n    - `Offset`, `Timestamp`, `StartOrEnd` - Modifiers\\n  \\n  - **`UnaryExpr`**: Unary operations\\n    - `Op ItemType` - Operator (+ or -)\\n    - `Expr Expr` - Operand\\n  \\n  - **`ParenExpr`**: Parenthesized expressions\\n    - `Expr Expr` - Inner expression\\n  \\n  - **`NumberLiteral`**: Numeric literals\\n    - `Val float64` - Numeric value\\n    - `Duration bool` - Whether formatted as duration\\n  \\n  - **`StringLiteral`**: String literals\\n    - `Val string` - String value\\n  \\n  - **`DurationExpr`**: Duration expressions for range/step\\n    - `Op ItemType` - Operation\\n    - `LHS, RHS Expr` - Operands\\n    - `StartPos, EndPos` - Position tracking\\n\\n- **`VectorMatching` struct**: Describes vector matching behavior\\n  - `Card VectorMatchCardinality` - One-to-one, many-to-one, one-to-many, many-to-many\\n  - `MatchingLabels []string` - Labels for matching\\n  - `On bool` - ON vs IGNORING modifier\\n  - `Include []string` - GROUP_LEFT/GROUP_RIGHT labels\\n  - `FillValues VectorMatchFillValues` - Fill modifier values\\n\\n- **`EvalStmt`**: Top-level evaluation statement\\n  - `Expr Expr` - Expression to evaluate\\n  - `Start, End time.Time` - Time range\\n  - `Interval time.Duration` - Step/interval\\n  - `LookbackDelta time.Duration` - Lookback window\\n\\n- **Helper functions**:\\n  - `Walk(v Visitor, node Node, path []Node)` - Tree traversal\\n  - `Inspect(node Node, f inspector)` - Depth-first inspection\\n  - `ChildrenIter(node Node)` - Iterate child nodes\\n  - `ExtractSelectors(expr Expr)` - Extract all metric selectors\\n\\n### YACC Parser Grammar\\n\\n**Files: `promql/parser/generated_parser.y` and `promql/parser/generated_parser.y.go`**\\n\\n- **`generated_parser.y`**: YACC grammar specification defining:\\n  - Token definitions and types\\n  - Grammar rules for PromQL syntax\\n  - Semantic actions for AST construction\\n  - Operator precedence and associativity\\n  - Support for multiple start symbols (expression, metric, series description, etc.)\\n\\n- **`generated_parser.y.go`**: Compiled YACC parser containing:\\n  - `yyParserImpl` struct - Parser state machine\\n  - `Parse()` method - Main parsing entry point\\n  - Lexer interface implementation\\n  - Token constants and value types\\n  - Symbol table and action tables\\n\\n### Function Registry\\n\\n**File: `promql/parser/functions.go`**\\n\\n- **`Function` struct**: Defines a PromQL function with:\\n  - `Name string` - Function name\\n  - `ArgTypes []ValueType` - Expected argument types\\n  - `Variadic int` - Number of variadic arguments allowed\\n  - `ReturnType ValueType` - Return type (Vector, Scalar, Matrix, String)\\n  - `Experimental bool` - Whether function is experimental\\n\\n- **`Functions` map**: Global registry of all ~100+ PromQL functions including:\\n  - Instant vector functions: `abs`, `ceil`, `floor`, `round`, `sqrt`, `log`, `exp`, `sin`, `cos`, `tan`, `asin`, `acos`, `atan`, `sinh`, `cosh`, `tanh`, etc.\\n  - Range vector functions: `rate`, `increase`, `delta`, `irate`, `idelta`, `changes`, `resets`, etc.\\n  - Aggregation functions: `sum`, `avg`, `count`, `min`, `max`, `group`, `stddev`, `stdvar`, `topk`, `bottomk`, `count_values`, `quantile`\\n  - Time functions: `time`, `hour`, `minute`, `second`, `day_of_month`, `day_of_week`, `day_of_year`, `month`, `year`, `days_in_month`\\n  - String functions: `label_join`, `label_replace`\\n  - Other: `scalar`, `vector`, `histogram_quantile`, `holt_winters`, `predict_linear`, `lte_histogram`, `gte_histogram`, `info`, etc.\\n\\n### Value Type System\\n\\n**File: `promql/parser/value.go`**\\n\\n- **`ValueType` type**: String-based enumeration of expression result types:\\n  - `ValueTypeVector` - Instant vector (time series at a single point)\\n  - `ValueTypeMatrix` - Range vector (time series over a time range)\\n  - `ValueTypeScalar` - Single numeric value\\n  - `ValueTypeString` - String value\\n  - `ValueTypeNone` - No value (error state)\\n\\n- **`Value` interface**: Generic interface for runtime values with:\\n  - `Type() ValueType` - Returns value type\\n  - `String() string` - String representation\\n\\n- **`DocumentedType(t ValueType)`**: Maps internal types to user-facing terminology\\n  - Vector → \\\"instant vector\\\"\\n  - Matrix → \\\"range vector\\\"\\n\\n### Engine Integration\\n\\n**File: `promql/engine.go`**\\n\\n- **`Engine` struct**: Main query execution engine that:\\n  - Holds a `parser parser.Parser` for parsing expressions\\n  - Manages query execution lifecycle\\n  - Enforces resource limits (max samples, timeout)\\n  - Tracks active queries\\n  - Logs query statistics\\n\\n- **`QueryEngine` interface**: Public interface for creating and executing queries\\n  - `NewInstantQuery()` - Create instant (point-in-time) query\\n  - `NewRangeQuery()` - Create range query\\n\\n- **`Query` interface**: Represents a parsed and executable query\\n  - `Statement() parser.Statement` - Get parsed AST\\n  - `Exec(ctx context.Context) *Result` - Execute query\\n  - `String() string` - Get original query string\\n  - `Stats() *stats.Statistics` - Get execution statistics\\n  - `Cancel()` - Cancel execution\\n  - `Close()` - Free resources\\n\\n- **`EngineOpts` struct**: Configuration for Engine including:\\n  - `Parser parser.Parser` - Custom parser instance\\n  - `Timeout time.Duration` - Query timeout\\n  - `MaxSamples int` - Maximum loaded samples\\n  - `LookbackDelta time.Duration` - Staleness delta\\n  - Feature flags for extended range selectors, binop fill modifiers, negative offsets, etc.\\n\\n### Runtime Value Types\\n\\n**File: `promql/value.go`**\\n\\n- **`Vector` type**: Slice of `Sample` objects representing instant vectors\\n  - Each `Sample` has: metric labels, timestamp, float value, histogram\\n\\n- **`Matrix` type**: Slice of `Series` objects representing range vectors\\n  - Each `Series` contains: metric labels, float points (`FPoint`), histogram points (`HPoint`)\\n\\n- **`Scalar` struct**: Single numeric value with timestamp\\n  - `T int64` - Millisecond timestamp\\n  - `V float64` - Numeric value\\n\\n- **`String` struct**: String value with timestamp\\n  - `T int64` - Millisecond timestamp\\n  - `V string` - String value\\n\\n- **`FPoint` struct**: Single float data point\\n  - `T int64` - Millisecond timestamp\\n  - `F float64` - Value\\n\\n- **`HPoint` struct**: Single histogram data point\\n  - `T int64` - Millisecond timestamp\\n  - `H *histogram.FloatHistogram` - Histogram value\\n\\n### Supporting Components\\n\\n**File: `promql/parser/features.go`**\\n\\n- **`RegisterFeatures(r features.Collector)`**: Registers all PromQL features with feature collector\\n  - Operators (arithmetic and comparison/set)\\n  - Aggregators (standard and experimental)\\n  - Keywords and modifiers\\n  - Functions\\n\\n**File: `promql/parser/printer.go`**\\n\\n- **`Tree(node Node) string`**: Returns ASCII tree representation of AST\\n- **String() methods**: Each AST node implements string generation for round-trip parsing\\n\\n**File: `promql/parser/prettier.go`**\\n\\n- **`PrettifyScript(s string)`**: Formats PromQL query for human readability\\n\\n**File: `promql/parser/posrange/posrange.go`**\\n\\n- **`PositionRange` struct**: Tracks source code positions for error reporting\\n  - `Start, End posrange.Pos` - Character positions in input\\n\\n**File: `promql/functions.go`**\\n\\n- **`FunctionCall` type**: Implementation type for PromQL function handlers\\n- Contains implementations of all built-in functions\\n\\n**File: `promql/info.go`**\\n\\n- **`evalInfo()`**: Special implementation of the `info()` function for target metadata queries\\n\\n**File: `promql/durations.go`**\\n\\n- Duration parsing and formatting utilities\\n- Supports Prometheus duration syntax (e.g., \\\"5m\\\", \\\"1h\\\", \\\"30s\\\")\\n\\n**File: `promql/query_logger.go`**\\n\\n- `QueryLogger` interface for logging executed queries\\n- Integration with JSON file logger\\n\\n## Processing Pipeline\\n\\nWhen a PromQL query is executed:\\n\\n1. **Engine** (promql/engine.go) receives the query string\\n2. **Parser.ParseExpr()** is called with the query\\n3. **Lexer** (promql/parser/lex.go) tokenizes the input → `Item` stream\\n4. **YACC Parser** (generated_parser.y.go) performs syntax analysis → constructs **AST** nodes (promql/parser/ast.go)\\n5. **checkAST()** performs semantic validation:\\n   - Traverses AST using `Walk()` or `ChildrenIter()`\\n   - Type checks each expression using `ValueType`\\n   - Validates operator usage and arity\\n   - Checks function argument types against **Function registry** (promql/parser/functions.go)\\n   - Validates vector matching clauses\\n6. **Engine** evaluates the validated AST against time series data\\n7. Results are accumulated as **runtime values** (Vector, Matrix, Scalar, String from promql/value.go)\\n\\n## Key Design Patterns\\n\\n1. **Parser Pooling**: `parserPool sync.Pool` reuses parser instances for efficiency\\n2. **Error Accumulation**: `ParseErrors []ParseErr` collects multiple parse errors instead of failing on first\\n3. **Visitor Pattern**: `Walk()` function enables custom AST traversal\\n4. **Feature Registry**: Tracks which PromQL features are enabled/disabled\\n5. **Position Tracking**: `PositionRange` enables precise error messages with line/column information\\n6. **Type Safety**: `ValueType` enum enforces expression type correctness at parse time\\n7. **Yacc State Machine**: Leverages GNU Yacc for robust, proven parsing technology\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":951,"cache_read_input_tokens":86172,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":951},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"0b197e48-fb9c-48bd-9d01-f07c169cef33","uuid":"f47ebe2f-43ab-4aa2-956e-bdbb0c08085e"}

implemented in the `github.com/prometheus/prometheus` repository across the `promql/` and `promql/parser/` directories. The pipeline follows a multi-stage architecture:\\n\\n1. **Lexical Analysis** (Tokenization)\\n2. **Syntax Analysis** (Parsing with Yacc)\\n3. **Abstract Syntax Tree (AST) Construction**\\n4. **Semantic Validation** (Type checking)\\n5. **Query Execution** (via the Engine)\\n\\n## Key Components\\n\\n### Parser Interface and Implementation\\n\\n**File: `promql/parser/parse.go`**\\n\\n- **`Parser` interface**: Defines the public API for PromQL parsing with methods:\\n  - `ParseExpr(input string) (Expr, error)` - Parses a PromQL expression\\n  - `ParseMetric(input string)` - Parses metric definitions\\n  - `ParseMetricSelector(input string)` - Parses metric label selectors\\n  - `ParseMetricSelectors(matchers []string)` - Parses multiple selectors\\n  - `ParseSeriesDesc(input string)` - Parses series descriptions for testing\\n  - `RegisterFeatures(r features.Collector)` - Registers PromQL features\\n\\n- **`parser` struct**: Low-level parser implementation that:\\n  - Manages the lexer state (`lex Lexer`)\\n  - Maintains function registry (`functions map[string]*Function`)\\n  - Handles YACC-generated parser (`yyParser yyParserImpl`)\\n  - Accumulates parsing errors (`parseErrors ParseErrors`)\\n  - Supports parser pooling for efficiency\\n\\n- **`checkAST(node Node) ValueType`**: Performs semantic validation and type checking on the AST including:\\n  - Recursive type validation for all expressions\\n  - Vector/scalar type enforcement\\n  - Aggregation operator validation\\n  - Binary operator and vector matching validation\\n  - Function call argument type checking\\n  - Label matcher validation\\n\\n### Lexer Tokenizer\\n\\n**File: `promql/parser/lex.go`**\\n\\n- **`Lexer` struct**: Implements tokenization with:\\n  - Input stream management (`input string`)\\n  - Position tracking (`pos`, `start`, `width`)\\n  - State machine support (`state stateFn`)\\n  - Nesting depth tracking for parentheses, braces, brackets\\n  - String and duration literal handling\\n  - Histogram description parsing support\\n\\n- **`Item` struct**: Represents a lexical token with:\\n  - Type (`ItemType`) - enumerated token types\\n  - Position (`posrange.Pos`)\\n  - Value (`Val string`) - actual token text\\n\\n- **`ItemType` enum**: Defines all token types including:\\n  - Operators: `ADD`, `SUB`, `MUL`, `DIV`, `MOD`, `POW`\\n  - Comparison: `EQLC`, `NEQ`, `LTE`, `GTE`, `LSS`, `GTR`\\n  - Set operators: `LAND`, `LOR`, `LUNLESS`\\n  - Aggregators: `SUM`, `AVG`, `COUNT`, `MIN`, `MAX`, `TOPK`, `BOTTOMK`, `QUANTILE`, etc.\\n  - Keywords: `OFFSET`, `BY`, `WITHOUT`, `ON`, `IGNORING`, `GROUP_LEFT`, `GROUP_RIGHT`, `BOOL`\\n  - Literals: `NUMBER`, `STRING`, `DURATION`, `IDENTIFIER`\\n  - Delimiters: `LEFT_PAREN`, `RIGHT_PAREN`, `LEFT_BRACE`, `RIGHT_BRACE`, `LEFT_BRACKET`, `RIGHT_BRACKET`\\n\\n- **`NextItem(itemp *Item)`**: Advances the lexer and populates the next token\\n\\n### AST Node Definitions\\n\\n**File: `promql/parser/ast.go`**\\n\\n- **`Node` interface**: Base interface for all AST nodes with methods:\\n  - `String() string` - Returns parseable string representation\\n  - `Pretty(level int) string` - Returns prettified representation\\n  - `PositionRange() posrange.PositionRange` - Returns source position\\n\\n- **`Expr` interface**: Base interface for all expressions implementing `Node` with:\\n  - `Type() ValueType` - Returns expression result type (Vector, Scalar, Matrix, String)\\n  - `PromQLExpr()` - Marker method\\n\\n- **Expression Types**:\\n  - **`VectorSelector`**: Represents metric selection with label matchers\\n    - `Name string` - Metric name\\n    - `LabelMatchers []*labels.Matcher` - Label match conditions\\n    - `OriginalOffset`, `Offset` - Offset modifier\\n    - `Timestamp`, `StartOrEnd` - @ modifier\\n    - `Anchored`, `Smoothed` - Extended range modifiers\\n  \\n  - **`MatrixSelector`**: Range vector selection\\n    - `VectorSelector Expr` - Base vector selector\\n    - `Range time.Duration` - Range duration\\n  \\n  - **`BinaryExpr`**: Binary operations\\n    - `Op ItemType` - Operator type\\n    - `LHS, RHS Expr` - Left and right operands\\n    - `VectorMatching *VectorMatching` - Vector cardinality matching\\n    - `ReturnBool bool` - Modifier for comparison operators\\n  \\n  - **`AggregateExpr`**: Aggregation operations\\n    - `Op ItemType` - Aggregator type (SUM, AVG, COUNT, etc.)\\n    - `Expr Expr` - Expression to aggregate\\n    - `Param Expr` - Optional parameter (for TOPK, BOTTOMK, etc.)\\n    - `Grouping []string` - BY/WITHOUT labels\\n    - `Without bool` - Without vs By modifier\\n  \\n  - **`Call`**: Function calls\\n    - `Func *Function` - Function definition\\n    - `Args Expressions` - Arguments\\n  \\n  - **`SubqueryExpr`**: Subqueries with range and step\\n    - `Expr Expr` - Inner expression\\n    - `Range time.Duration` - Range duration\\n    - `Step time.Duration` - Step duration\\n    - `Offset`, `Timestamp`, `StartOrEnd` - Modifiers\\n  \\n  - **`UnaryExpr`**: Unary operations\\n    - `Op ItemType` - Operator (+ or -)\\n    - `Expr Expr` - Operand\\n  \\n  - **`ParenExpr`**: Parenthesized expressions\\n    - `Expr Expr` - Inner expression\\n  \\n  - **`NumberLiteral`**: Numeric literals\\n    - `Val float64` - Numeric value\\n    - `Duration bool` - Whether formatted as duration\\n  \\n  - **`StringLiteral`**: String literals\\n    - `Val string` - String value\\n  \\n  - **`DurationExpr`**: Duration expressions for range/step\\n    - `Op ItemType` - Operation\\n    - `LHS, RHS Expr` - Operands\\n    - `StartPos, EndPos` - Position tracking\\n\\n- **`VectorMatching` struct**: Describes vector matching behavior\\n  - `Card VectorMatchCardinality` - One-to-one, many-to-one, one-to-many, many-to-many\\n  - `MatchingLabels []string` - Labels for matching\\n  - `On bool` - ON vs IGNORING modifier\\n  - `Include []string` - GROUP_LEFT/GROUP_RIGHT labels\\n  - `FillValues VectorMatchFillValues` - Fill modifier values\\n\\n- **`EvalStmt`**: Top-level evaluation statement\\n  - `Expr Expr` - Expression to evaluate\\n  - `Start, End time.Time` - Time range\\n  - `Interval time.Duration` - Step/interval\\n  - `LookbackDelta time.Duration` - Lookback window\\n\\n- **Helper functions**:\\n  - `Walk(v Visitor, node Node, path []Node)` - Tree traversal\\n  - `Inspect(node Node, f inspector)` - Depth-first inspection\\n  - `ChildrenIter(node Node)` - Iterate child nodes\\n  - `ExtractSelectors(expr Expr)` - Extract all metric selectors\\n\\n### YACC Parser Grammar\\n\\n**Files: `promql/parser/generated_parser.y` and `promql/parser/generated_parser.y.go`**\\n\\n- **`generated_parser.y`**: YACC grammar specification defining:\\n  - Token definitions and types\\n  - Grammar rules for PromQL syntax\\n  - Semantic actions for AST construction\\n  - Operator precedence and associativity\\n  - Support for multiple start symbols (expression, metric, series description, etc.)\\n\\n- **`generated_parser.y.go`**: Compiled YACC parser containing:\\n  - `yyParserImpl` struct - Parser state machine\\n  - `Parse()` method - Main parsing entry point\\n  - Lexer interface implementation\\n  - Token constants and value types\\n  - Symbol table and action tables\\n\\n### Function Registry\\n\\n**File: `promql/parser/functions.go`**\\n\\n- **`Function` struct**: Defines a PromQL function with:\\n  - `Name string` - Function name\\n  - `ArgTypes []ValueType` - Expected argument types\\n  - `Variadic int` - Number of variadic arguments allowed\\n  - `ReturnType ValueType` - Return type (Vector, Scalar, Matrix, String)\\n  - `Experimental bool` - Whether function is experimental\\n\\n- **`Functions` map**: Global registry of all ~100+ PromQL functions including:\\n  - Instant vector functions: `abs`, `ceil`, `floor`, `round`, `sqrt`, `log`, `exp`, `sin`, `cos`, `tan`, `asin`, `acos`, `atan`, `sinh`, `cosh`, `tanh`, etc.\\n  - Range vector functions: `rate`, `increase`, `delta`, `irate`, `idelta`, `changes`, `resets`, etc.\\n  - Aggregation functions: `sum`, `avg`, `count`, `min`, `max`, `group`, `stddev`, `stdvar`, `topk`, `bottomk`, `count_values`, `quantile`\\n  - Time functions: `time`, `hour`, `minute`, `second`, `day_of_month`, `day_of_week`, `day_of_year`, `month`, `year`, `days_in_month`\\n  - String functions: `label_join`, `label_replace`\\n  - Other: `scalar`, `vector`, `histogram_quantile`, `holt_winters`, `predict_linear`, `lte_histogram`, `gte_histogram`, `info`, etc.\\n\\n### Value Type System\\n\\n**File: `promql/parser/value.go`**\\n\\n- **`ValueType` type**: String-based enumeration of expression result types:\\n  - `ValueTypeVector` - Instant vector (time series at a single point)\\n  - `ValueTypeMatrix` - Range vector (time series over a time range)\\n  - `ValueTypeScalar` - Single numeric value\\n  - `ValueTypeString` - String value\\n  - `ValueTypeNone` - No value (error state)\\n\\n- **`Value` interface**: Generic interface for runtime values with:\\n  - `Type() ValueType` - Returns value type\\n  - `String() string` - String representation\\n\\n- **`DocumentedType(t ValueType)`**: Maps internal types to user-facing terminology\\n  - Vector → \\\"instant vector\\\"\\n  - Matrix → \\\"range vector\\\"\\n\\n### Engine Integration\\n\\n**File: `promql/engine.go`**\\n\\n- **`Engine` struct**: Main query execution engine that:\\n  - Holds a `parser parser.Parser` for parsing expressions\\n  - Manages query execution lifecycle\\n  - Enforces resource limits (max samples, timeout)\\n  - Tracks active queries\\n  - Logs query statistics\\n\\n- **`QueryEngine` interface**: Public interface for creating and executing queries\\n  - `NewInstantQuery()` - Create instant (point-in-time) query\\n  - `NewRangeQuery()` - Create range query\\n\\n- **`Query` interface**: Represents a parsed and executable query\\n  - `Statement() parser.Statement` - Get parsed AST\\n  - `Exec(ctx context.Context) *Result` - Execute query\\n  - `String() string` - Get original query string\\n  - `Stats() *stats.Statistics` - Get execution statistics\\n  - `Cancel()` - Cancel execution\\n  - `Close()` - Free resources\\n\\n- **`EngineOpts` struct**: Configuration for Engine including:\\n  - `Parser parser.Parser` - Custom parser instance\\n  - `Timeout time.Duration` - Query timeout\\n  - `MaxSamples int` - Maximum loaded samples\\n  - `LookbackDelta time.Duration` - Staleness delta\\n  - Feature flags for extended range selectors, binop fill modifiers, negative offsets, etc.\\n\\n### Runtime Value Types\\n\\n**File: `promql/value.go`**\\n\\n- **`Vector` type**: Slice of `Sample` objects representing instant vectors\\n  - Each `Sample` has: metric labels, timestamp, float value, histogram\\n\\n- **`Matrix` type**: Slice of `Series` objects representing range vectors\\n  - Each `Series` contains: metric labels, float points (`FPoint`), histogram points (`HPoint`)\\n\\n- **`Scalar` struct**: Single numeric value with timestamp\\n  - `T int64` - Millisecond timestamp\\n  - `V float64` - Numeric value\\n\\n- **`String` struct**: String value with timestamp\\n  - `T int64` - Millisecond timestamp\\n  - `V string` - String value\\n\\n- **`FPoint` struct**: Single float data point\\n  - `T int64` - Millisecond timestamp\\n  - `F float64` - Value\\n\\n- **`HPoint` struct**: Single histogram data point\\n  - `T int64` - Millisecond timestamp\\n  - `H *histogram.FloatHistogram` - Histogram value\\n\\n### Supporting Components\\n\\n**File: `promql/parser/features.go`**\\n\\n- **`RegisterFeatures(r features.Collector)`**: Registers all PromQL features with feature collector\\n  - Operators (arithmetic and comparison/set)\\n  - Aggregators (standard and experimental)\\n  - Keywords and modifiers\\n  - Functions\\n\\n**File: `promql/parser/printer.go`**\\n\\n- **`Tree(node Node) string`**: Returns ASCII tree representation of AST\\n- **String() methods**: Each AST node implements string generation for round-trip parsing\\n\\n**File: `promql/parser/prettier.go`**\\n\\n- **`PrettifyScript(s string)`**: Formats PromQL query for human readability\\n\\n**File: `promql/parser/posrange/posrange.go`**\\n\\n- **`PositionRange` struct**: Tracks source code positions for error reporting\\n  - `Start, End posrange.Pos` - Character positions in input\\n\\n**File: `promql/functions.go`**\\n\\n- **`FunctionCall` type**: Implementation type for PromQL function handlers\\n- Contains implementations of all built-in functions\\n\\n**File: `promql/info.go`**\\n\\n- **`evalInfo()`**: Special implementation of the `info()` function for target metadata queries\\n\\n**File: `promql/durations.go`**\\n\\n- Duration parsing and formatting utilities\\n- Supports Prometheus duration syntax (e.g., \\\"5m\\\", \\\"1h\\\", \\\"30s\\\")\\n\\n**File: `promql/query_logger.go`**\\n\\n- `QueryLogger` interface for logging executed queries\\n- Integration with JSON file logger\\n\\n## Processing Pipeline\\n\\nWhen a PromQL query is executed:\\n\\n1. **Engine** (promql/engine.go) receives the query string\\n2. **Parser.ParseExpr()** is called with the query\\n3. **Lexer** (promql/parser/lex.go) tokenizes the input → `Item` stream\\n4. **YACC Parser** (generated_parser.y.go) performs syntax analysis → constructs **AST** nodes (promql/parser/ast.go)\\n5. **checkAST()** performs semantic validation:\\n   - Traverses AST using `Walk()` or `ChildrenIter()`\\n   - Type checks each expression using `ValueType`\\n   - Validates operator usage and arity\\n   - Checks function argument types against **Function registry** (promql/parser/functions.go)\\n   - Validates vector matching clauses\\n6. **Engine** evaluates the validated AST against time series data\\n7. Results are accumulated as **runtime values** (Vector, Matrix, Scalar, String from promql/value.go)\\n\\n## Key Design Patterns\\n\\n1. **Parser Pooling**: `parserPool sync.Pool` reuses parser instances for efficiency\\n2. **Error Accumulation**: `ParseErrors []ParseErr` collects multiple parse errors instead of failing on first\\n3. **Visitor Pattern**: `Walk()` function enables custom AST traversal\\n4. **Feature Registry**: Tracks which PromQL features are enabled/disabled\\n5. **Position Tracking**: `PositionRange` enables precise error messages with line/column information\\n6. **Type Safety**: `ValueType` enum enforces expression type correctness at parse time\\n7. **Yacc State Machine**: Leverages GNU Yacc for robust, proven parsing technology\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
